  public byte[] evaluateResponse(byte[] response) throws SaslException, SaslAuthenticationException {\n    98→        try {\n    99→            switch (state) {\n   100→                case                       throw new SaslAuthenticationException(\"Authentication failed: Client requested an authorization id that is different from username\");\n   133→\n   134→ \" + mechanism.minIterations() + \" for \" + mechanism);\n   136→                        this.serverFirstMessage = new ServerFirstMessage(clientFirstMessage.nonce(),\n   137→                                serverNonce,\n   138→                                scramCredential.salt(),\n   139→                                scramCredential.iterations());\n   140→                        setState(State.RECEIVE_CLIENT_FINAL_MESSAGE);\n   141→                        return serverFirstMessage.toBytes();\n   142→                    } catch (SaslException | AuthenticationException e) {\n            return toMessage().getBytes(StandardCharsets.UTF_8);\n        }\n\n        protected String toMessage(byte[] messageBytes) {\n            return new String(messageBytes, authorizationId;\n        private final ScramExtensions extensions;\n        public ClientFirstMessage(byte[] messageBytes) throws SaslException {\n            String message = format: \" + message);\n            String authzid = matcher.group(\"authzid\");\n            this.authorizationId = authzid != null ? authzid : \"\";\n            this.saslName = matcher.group(\"saslname\");\n            this.nonce = matcher.group(\"nonce\");\n            String extString = matcher.group(\"extensions\");\n\n            this.extensions = extString.startsWith(\",\") ? new ScramExtensions(extString.substring(1)) : new ScramExtensions();\n        }\n        public ClientFirstMessage(String saslName, String nonce, Map<String, String> + serverNonce;\n            this.salt = salt;\n            this.iterations = iterations;\n        }\n        public String nonce() {\n            return nonce;\n        }\n        public byte[] salt() {\n            return salt;\n        }\n        public int iterations() {\n            return iterations;\n        }\n        String toMessage() {\n            return String.format(\"r=%s,s=%s,i=%d\", nonce, Base64.getEncoder().encodeToString(salt), iterations);\n        }\n    }\n    /**\n     * Format:\n     *     channel-binding \",\" nonce [\",\" extensions]\",\" proof\n     * Limitations:\n     *     Extensions are ignored.\n     *\n     */\n    public static class ClientFinalMessage extends AbstractScramMessage {\n        private static final Pattern PATTERN = Pattern.compile(String.format(\n                \"c=(?<channel>%s),r=(?<nonce>%s)%s,p=(?<proof>%s)\",\n                BASE64,\n                PRINTABLE,\n                EXTENSIONS,\n                BASE64));\n\n        private final byte[] channelBinding;\n        private final String nonce;\n        private byte[] proof;\n        public ClientFinalMessage(byte[] messageBytes) throws matcher.group(\"nonce\");\n            this.proof = Base64.getDecoder().decode(matcher.group(\"proof\"));\n        }\n        public ClientFinalMessage(byte[] channelBinding, String nonce) {\n        this.error = error;\n            this.serverSignature = serverSignature;\n        }\n        public String error() {\n            return error;\n        }\n        public byte[] Logger LOG = LoggerFactory.getLogger(SaslServerAuthenticator.class);\n    95→\n    96→    /**\n    97→     * The internal state transitions for initial authentication of a channel on the\n    98→     * server side are declared in order, starting with {@link #INITIAL_REQUEST} and\n    99→     * ending in either {@link #COMPLETE} or {@link #FAILED}.\n   100→     * <p>\n   101→     * Re-authentication of a channel on the server side starts with the state\n   102→     * {@link #REAUTH_PROCESS_HANDSHAKE}. It may then flow to\n   103→     * {@link #REAUTH_BAD_MECHANISM} before a transition to {@link #FAILED} if\n   104→     * re-authentication is attempted with a mechanism different than the original\n   105→     * one; otherwise it joins the authentication flow at the {@link #AUTHENTICATE}\n   106→     * state and likewise ends at either {@link #COMPLETE} or {@link #FAILED}.\n   107→     */\n   108→    private enum SaslState {\n   109→        INITIAL_REQUEST,               // May be SaslHandshake or ApiVersions for authentication\n   110→        HANDSHAKE_OR_VERSIONS_REQUEST, // May be SaslHandshake or ApiVersions\n   111→        HANDSHAKE_REQUEST,             // After an ApiVersions request, next request must be SaslHandshake\n   112→        AUTHENTICATE,                  // Authentication tokens (SaslHandshake v1 and above indicate SaslAuthenticate headers)\n   113→        COMPLETE,                      // Authentication completed successfully\n   114→        FAILED,                        // Authentication failed\n   115→        REAUTH_PROCESS_HANDSHAKE,      // Initial state for re-authentication, processes SASL handshake request\n   116→        REAUTH_BAD_MECHANISM,          // When re-authentication requested with wrong mechanism, generate exception\n   117→    }\n   118→\n   119→    private final SecurityProtocol securityProtocol;\n   120→    private final ListenerName listenerName;\n   121→    private final String connectionId;\n   122→    private final Map<String, Subject> subjects;\n   123→    private final TransportLayer transportLayer;\n   124→    private final List<String> enabledMechanisms;\n   125→    private final Map<String, ?> configs;\n   126→    private final KafkaPrincipalBuilder principalBuilder;\n   127→    private final Map<String, AuthenticateCallbackHandler> callbackHandlers;\n   128→    private final Map<String, Long> connectionsMaxReauthMsByMechanism;\n   129→    private final Time time;\n   130→    private final ReauthInfo reauthInfo;\n   131→    private final ChannelMetadataRegistry metadataRegistry;\n   132→    private final Function<Short, ApiVersionsResponse> apiVersionSupplier;\n   133→\n   134→    // Current SASL state\n   135→    private SaslState saslState = SaslState.INITIAL_REQUEST;\n   136→    // Next SASL state to be set when outgoing writes associated with the current SASL state complete\n   137→    private SaslState pendingSaslState = null;\n   138→    // Exception that will be thrown by `authenticate()` when SaslState is set to FAILED after outbound writes complete\n   139→    private AuthenticationException pendingException = null;\n   140→    private SaslServer saslServer;\n   141→    private String saslMechanism;\n   142→\n   143→    // buffers used in                 String connectionId,\n   154→                                   Map<String, Subject> subjects,\n   155→                                   KerberosShortNamer kerberosNameParser,\n List<String> enabledMechanisms = (List<String>) this.configs.get(BrokerSecurityConfigs.SASL_ENABLED_MECHANISMS_CONFIG);\n   179→        if (enabledMechanisms == null || enabledMechanisms.isEmpty())\n   180→            throw new IllegalArgumentException(\"No SASL mechanisms are enabled\");\n   181→        this.enabledMechanisms = new ArrayList<>(new HashSet<>(enabledMechanisms));\n   182→        for specified for SASL mechanism \" + mechanism);\n   185→            if (!subjects.containsKey(mechanism))\n   186→                throw new IllegalArgumentException(\"Subject cannot be null for SASL mechanism \" + mechanism);\n   187→            LOG.trace(\"{} for mechanism={}: {}\", BrokerSecurityConfigs.CONNECTIONS_MAX_REAUTH_MS_CONFIG, mechanism,\n   188→                    connectionsMaxReauthMsByMechanism.get(mechanism));\n   189→        }\n   190→\n   191→        // Note that the old principal builder does not support SASL, so we do not need to pass the\n   192→        // authenticator or the transport layer\n   193→        this.principalBuilder = ChannelBuilders.createPrincipalBuilder(configs, kerberosNameParser, null);\n   194→\n   195→        saslAuthRequestMaxReceiveSize = (Integer) configs.get(BrokerSecurityConfigs.SASL_SERVER_MAX_RECEIVE_SIZE_CONFIG);\n   196→        if (saslAuthRequestMaxReceiveSize == null)\n   197→            saslAuthRequestMaxReceiveSize = BrokerSecurityConfigs.DEFAULT_SASL_SERVER_MAX_RECEIVE_SIZE;\n   198→    }\n   199→\n   200→    private void createSaslServer(String mechanism) throws IOException {\n   201→        this.saslMechanism = mechanism;\n   202→        Subject subject = subjects.get(mechanism);\n   203→        final AuthenticateCallbackHandler callbackHandler = callbackHandlers.get(mechanism);\n   204→        if (mechanism.equals(SaslConfigs.GSSAPI_MECHANISM)) {\n   205→            saslServer = createSaslKerberosServer(callbackHandler, configs, subject);\n   206→        } else {\n   207→            try {\n   208→                saslServer = SecurityManagerCompatibility.get().callAs(subject, () ->\n   209→                    Sasl.createSaslServer(saslMechanism, \"kafka\", serverAddress().getHostName(), configs, callbackHandler));\n   210→                if (saslServer == null) {\n   211→                    throw new SaslException(\"Kafka Server failed to create a SaslServer to interact with a client during session authentication with server mechanism \" + saslMechanism);\n   212→                }\n   213→            } catch (CompletionException e) {\n   214→                throw new SaslException(\"Kafka Server failed to create a SaslServer to interact with a client during session authentication with server mechanism \" + saslMechanism, e.getCause());\n   215→            }\n   216→        }\n   217→    }\n   218→\n   219→    private SaslServer createSaslKerberosServer(final AuthenticateCallbackHandler saslServerCallbackHandler, final Map<String, ?> configs, Subject subject) throws IOException {\n   220→        // server is using a JAAS-authenticated subject: determine service principal name and hostname from kafka server's subject.\n   221→        final String servicePrincipal = SaslClientAuthenticator.firstPrincipal(subject);\n   222→        KerberosName kerberosName;\n   223→        try {\n   224→            kerberosName = KerberosName.parse(servicePrincipal);\n   225→        } catch (IllegalArgumentException e) {\n   226→            throw new KafkaException(\"Principal has name with unexpected format \" + servicePrincipal);\n   227→        }\n   228→        final String servicePrincipalName = kerberosName.serviceName();\n   229→        final String serviceHostname = kerberosName.hostName();\n   230→\n   231→        LOG.debug(\"Creating SaslServer for {} with mechanism {}\", kerberosName, saslMechanism);\n   232→\n   233→        try {\n   234→            return SecurityManagerCompatibility.get().callAs(subject, () ->\n   235→                    Sasl.createSaslServer(saslMechanism, servicePrincipalName, serviceHostname, configs, saslServerCallbackHandler));\n   236→        } catch (CompletionException e) {\n   237→            throw new SaslException(\"Kafka Server failed to create a SaslServer to interact with a client during session authentication\", e.getCause());\n   238→        }\n   239→    }\n   240→\n   241→    /**\n   242→     * Evaluates client responses via `SaslServer.evaluateResponse` and returns the issued challenge to the client until\n   243→     * authentication succeeds or fails.\n   244→     *\n   245→     * The messages are sent and received as size delimited bytes that consists of a 4 byte network-ordered size N\n   246→     * followed by N bytes representing the opaque payload.\n   247→     */\n   248→    @SuppressWarnings(\"fallthrough\")\n   249→    @Override\n   250→    public void authenticate() throws IOException {\n   251→        if (saslState != SaslState.REAUTH_PROCESS_HANDSHAKE) {\n   252→            if (netOutBuffer != null && !flushNetOutBufferAndUpdateInterestOps())\n   253→                return;\n   254→\n   255→            if (saslServer != null && saslServer.isComplete()) {\n   256→                setSaslState(SaslState.COMPLETE);\n   257→                return;\n   258→            }\n   259→\n   260→            // allocate on heap (as opposed to any socket server memory pool)\n   261→            if (netInBuffer == null) netInBuffer = new NetworkReceive(saslAuthRequestMaxReceiveSize, connectionId);\n   262→\n   263→            try {\n   264→                netInBuffer.readFrom(transportLayer);\n   265→            } catch (InvalidReceiveException e) {\n   266→                throw new SaslAuthenticationException(\"Failing SASL authentication due to invalid receive size\", e);\n   267→            }\n   268→            if (!netInBuffer.complete())\n   269→                return;\n   270→            netInBuffer.payload().rewind();\n   271→        }\n   272→        byte[] clientToken = new byte[netInBuffer.payload().remaining()];\n   273→        netInBuffer.payload().get(clientToken, 0, clientToken.length);\n   274→        netInBuffer = null; // reset the networkReceive as we read all the data.\n   275→        try {\n   276→            switch (saslState) {\n   277→                case REAUTH_PROCESS_HANDSHAKE:\n   278→                case HANDSHAKE_OR_VERSIONS_REQUEST:\n   279→                case HANDSHAKE_REQUEST:\n   280→                case INITIAL_REQUEST:\n   281→                    handleKafkaRequest(clientToken);\n   282→                    break;\n   283→                case REAUTH_BAD_MECHANISM:\n   284→                    throw new SaslAuthenticationException(reauthInfo.badMechanismErrorMessage);\n   285→                case AUTHENTICATE:\n   286→                    handleSaslToken(clientToken);\n   287→                    // When the authentication exchange is complete and no more tokens are expected from the client,\n   288→                    // update SASL state. Current SASL state will be updated when outgoing writes to the client complete.\n   289→                    if (saslServer.isComplete())\n   290→                        setSaslState(SaslState.COMPLETE);\n   291→                    break;\n   292→                default:\n   293→                    break;\n   294→            }\n   295→        } catch (AuthenticationException e) {\n   296→            // Exception will be propagated after response is sent to client\n   297→            setSaslState(SaslState.FAILED, e);\n   298→        } catch (Exception e) {\n   299→            // In the case of IOExceptions and other unexpected exceptions, fail immediately\n   300→            saslState = SaslState.FAILED;\n   301→            LOG.debug(\"Failed during {}: {}\", reauthInfo.authenticationOrReauthenticationText(), e.getMessage());\n   302→            throw e;\n   303→        }\n   304→    }\n   305→\n   306→    @Override\n   307→    public KafkaPrincipal principal() {\n   308→        Optional<SSLSession> sslSession = transportLayer instanceof SslTransportLayer ?\n   309→                Optional.of(((SslTransportLayer) transportLayer).sslSession()) : Optional.empty();\n   310→        SaslAuthenticationContext context = new SaslAuthenticationContext(saslServer, securityProtocol,\n   311→                clientAddress(), listenerName.value(), sslSession);\n   312→        KafkaPrincipal principal = principalBuilder.build(context);\n   313→        if (ScramMechanism.isScram(saslMechanism) && Boolean.parseBoolean((String) saslServer.getNegotiatedProperty(ScramLoginModule.TOKEN_AUTH_CONFIG))) {\n   314→            principal.tokenAuthenticated(true);\n   315→        }\n   316→        return principal;\n   317→    }\n   318→\n   319→    @Override\n   320→    public Optional<KafkaPrincipalSerde> principalSerde() {\n   321→        return principalBuilder instanceof KafkaPrincipalSerde ? @Override\n   343→    public void reauthenticate(ReauthenticationContext reauthenticationContext) throws IOException {\n   344→        NetworkReceive saslHandshakeReceive = 377→\n   378→    private void setSaslState(SaslState saslState, AuthenticationException exception) {\n   379→        if (netOutBuffer != null && !netOutBuffer.completed()) {\n   380→        if (exception != null)\n   388→                throw exception;\n   389→        }\n   390→    }\n   391→\n   392→    private boolean flushNetOutBufferAndUpdateInterestOps() throws IOException {\n   393→        boolean flushedCompletely = flushNetOutBuffer();\n   394→        if (flushedCompletely) {\n   395→            transportLayer.removeInterestOps(SelectionKey.OP_WRITE);\n   396→            if (pendingSaslState != null)\n   397→                setSaslState(pendingSaslState, pendingException);\n   398→        } else\n   399→            transportLayer.addInterestOps(SelectionKey.OP_WRITE);\n   400→        return flushedCompletely;\n   401→    }\n   402→\n   403→    private boolean flushNetOutBuffer() throws IOException {\n   404→ 419→    }\n   420→\n   421→    private void handleSaslToken(byte[] clientToken) throws IOException {\n   422→        if (!enableKafkaSaslAuthenticateHeaders) {\n   423→            byte[] response = saslServer.evaluateResponse(clientToken);\n   424→            if (saslServer.isComplete()) {\n   425→                reauthInfo.calcCompletionTimesAndReturnSessionLifetimeMs();\n   426→ 437→            short version = header.apiVersion();\n   438→            RequestContext requestContext = new RequestContext(header, connectionId, clientAddress(), Optional.of(clientPort()),\n   439→                    KafkaPrincipal.ANONYMOUS, listenerName, securityProtocol, ClientInformation.EMPTY, false);\n   440→            RequestAndSize requestAndSize = requestContext.parseRequest(requestBuffer);\n   441→            if (apiKey != ApiKeys.SASL_AUTHENTICATE) {\n   442→                IllegalSaslStateException e = new requestAndSize.request.getErrorResponse(e));\n   444→                throw e;\n   445→            }\n   446→            if (!apiKey.isVersionSupported(version)) {\n   447→                // We cannot create an error response if the request version of SaslAuthenticate is not supported\n   448→                // This should not normally occur since clients typically check supported versions using ApiVersionsRequest\n   449→                throw new UnsupportedVersionException(\"Version \" + version + \" is not supported for apiKey \" + apiKey);\n   450→            }\n   451→            /*\n   452→             * The client sends multiple SASL_AUTHENTICATE requests, and the client is known\n   453→             * to support the required version if any one of them indicates it supports that\n   454→             * version.\n   455→             */\n   456→            if (!reauthInfo.connectedClientSupportsReauthentication)\n   457→                reauthInfo.connectedClientSupportsReauthentication = version > 0;\n   458→            SaslAuthenticateRequest saslAuthenticateRequest = (SaslAuthenticateRequest) requestAndSize.request;\n   459→\n   460→            try {\n   461→                byte[] responseToken = saslServer.evaluateResponse(\n   462→                        Utils.copyArray(saslAuthenticateRequest.data().authBytes()));\n   463→ This avoids\n   514→            // unnecessary exposure to some of the more complex schema types.\n   515→            if (apiKey != ApiKeys.API_VERSIONS && apiKey != ApiKeys.SASL_HANDSHAKE)\n   516→                throw new InvalidRequestException(\"Unexpected Kafka request of type \" + apiKey + \" during SASL handshake.\");\n   517→\n   518→            LOG.debug(\"Handling Kafka request {} during {}\", apiKey, reauthInfo.authenticationOrReauthenticationText());\n   519→\n   520→            RequestContext requestContext = new RequestContext(header, connectionId, clientAddress(), Optional.of(clientPort()),\n   521→                    KafkaPrincipal.ANONYMOUS, listenerName, securityProtocol, ClientInformation.EMPTY, false);\n   522→            RequestAndSize requestAndSize = requestContext.parseRequest(requestBuffer);\n   523→\n   524→            // A valid Kafka request was received, we can now update the sasl state\n   525→            if (saslState == SaslState.INITIAL_REQUEST)\n   526→                setSaslState(SaslState.HANDSHAKE_OR_VERSIONS_REQUEST);\n   527→\n   528→            if (apiKey == ApiKeys.API_VERSIONS)\n   529→                handleApiVersionsRequest(requestContext, (ApiVersionsRequest) requestAndSize.request);\n   530→            else {\n   531→                String clientMechanism = handleHandshakeRequest(requestContext, (SaslHandshakeRequest) requestAndSize.request);\n   532→                if (!reauthInfo.reauthenticating() || reauthInfo.saslMechanismUnchanged(clientMechanism)) {\n   533→                    createSaslServer(clientMechanism);\n   534→                    setSaslState(SaslState.AUTHENTICATE);\n   535→                }\n   536→            }\n   537→        } catch (InvalidRequestException e) {\n   538→            if (saslState == SaslState.INITIAL_REQUEST) {\n   539→                // InvalidRequestException is thrown if the request is not in Kafka format or if the API key is invalid.\n   540→                // If it's the initial request, this could be an ancient client (see method documentation for more details),\n   541→                // a client configured with the wrong security protocol or a non kafka-client altogether (eg http client).\n   542→                throw new InvalidRequestException(\"Invalid request, potential reasons: kafka client configured with the \" +\n   543→                    \"wrong security protocol, it does not support KIP-43 or it is not a kafka client.\", e);\n   544→            }\n   545→            throw e;\n   546→        }\n   547→    }\n   548→\n   549→    private String handleHandshakeRequest(RequestContext context, SaslHandshakeRequest handshakeRequest) throws IOException, UnsupportedSaslMechanismException {\n   550→        String clientMechanism = handshakeRequest.data().mechanism();\n   551→        short version = context.header.apiVersion();\n   552→        if         new SaslHandshakeResponseData().setErrorCode(Errors.UNSUPPORTED_SASL_MECHANISM.code()).setMechanisms(enabledMechanisms)));\n   563→            throw new UnsupportedSaslMechanismException(\"Unsupported SASL mechanism \" + clientMechanism);\n   564→        }\n   565→    }\n   566→\n   567→    // Visible to override for testing\n   568→    protected void      long retvalSessionLifetimeMs = 0L;\n   669→            long authenticationEndMs = time.milliseconds();\n   670→            authenticationEndNanos = time.nanoseconds();\n   671→            Long zeroIfNegative(connectionsMaxReauthMs);\n   679→                else if (!maxReauthSet)\n   680→                    retvalSessionLifetimeMs = zeroIfNegative(credentialExpirationMs - authenticationEndMs);\n   681→                else\n   682→                    retvalSessionLifetimeMs = zeroIfNegative(Math.min(credentialExpirationMs - authenticationEndMs, retvalSessionLifetimeMs);\n   694→            } else {\n   695→                if (sessionExpirationTimeNanos != null)\n   696→                    LOG.debug(\n   697→ 712→            long latencyNanos = authenticationEndNanos - reauthenticationBeginNanos;\n   713→            return latencyNanos == 0L ? 0L : Math.max(1L, Math.round(latencyNanos / 1000.0 / 1000.0));\n   714→        }\n   715→\n   716→        private long zeroIfNegative(long value) {\n   717→            return Math.max(0L, value);\n   718→        }        \n   719→    }\n   720→}\n org.apache.kafka.common.requests.RequestAndSize;\nimport org.apache.kafka.common.requests.RequestContext;\nimport org.apache.kafka.common.requests.RequestHeader;\nimport org.apache.kafka.common.requests.SaslAuthenticateRequest;\nimport org.apache.kafka.common.requests.SaslAuthenticateResponse;\nimport org.apache.kafka.common.requests.SaslHandshakeRequest;\nimport org.apache.kafka.common.requests.SaslHandshakeResponse;\nimport org.apache.kafka.common.security.auth.AuthenticateCallbackHandler;\nimport org.apache.kafka.common.security.auth.KafkaPrincipal;\nimport org.apache.kafka.common.security.auth.KafkaPrincipalBuilder;\nimport org.apache.kafka.common.security.auth.KafkaPrincipalSerde;\nimport org.apache.kafka.common.security.auth.SaslAuthenticationContext;\nimport org.apache.kafka.common.security.auth.SecurityProtocol;\nimport org.apache.kafka.common.security.kerberos.KerberosError;\nimport org.apache.kafka.common.security.kerberos.KerberosName;\nimport org.apache.kafka.common.security.kerberos.KerberosShortNamer;\nimport org.apache.kafka.common.security.scram.ScramLoginModule;\nimport org.apache.kafka.common.security.scram.internals.ScramMechanism;\nimport org.apache.kafka.common.utils.Time;\nimport org.apache.kafka.common.utils.Utils;\n\nimport org.slf4j.Logger;\nimport org.slf4j.LoggerFactory;\n\nimport java.io.Closeable;\nimport java.io.IOException;\nimport java.net.InetAddress;\nimport java.nio.ByteBuffer;\nimport java.nio.channels.SelectionKey;\nimport java.util.ArrayList;\nimport java.util.Date;\nimport java.util.HashSet;\nimport java.util.List;\nimport java.util.Map;\nimport java.util.Objects;\nimport java.util.Optional;\nimport java.util.concurrent.CompletionException;\nimport java.util.function.Function;\n\nimport javax.net.ssl.SSLSession;\nimport javax.security.auth.Subject;\nimport javax.security.sasl.Sasl;\nimport javax.security.sasl.SaslException;\nimport javax.security.sasl.SaslServer;\n\npublic class SaslServerAuthenticator implements Authenticator {\n    private static final Logger LOG = LoggerFactory.getLogger(SaslServerAuthenticator.class);\n\n    /**\n     * The internal state transitions for initial authentication of a channel on the\n     * server side are declared in order, starting with {@link #INITIAL_REQUEST} and\n     * ending in either {@link #COMPLETE} or {@link #FAILED}.\n     * <p>\n     * Re-authentication of a channel on the server side starts with the state\n     * {@link #REAUTH_PROCESS_HANDSHAKE}. It may then flow to\n     * {@link #REAUTH_BAD_MECHANISM} before a transition to {@link #FAILED} if\n     * re-authentication is attempted with a mechanism different than the original\n     * one; otherwise it joins the authentication flow at the {@link #AUTHENTICATE}\n     * state and likewise ends at either {@link #COMPLETE} or {@link #FAILED}.\n     */\n    private enum SaslState {\n        INITIAL_REQUEST,               // May be SaslHandshake or ApiVersions for authentication\n        HANDSHAKE_OR_VERSIONS_REQUEST, // May be SaslHandshake or ApiVersions\n        HANDSHAKE_REQUEST,             // After an ApiVersions request, next request must be SaslHandshake\n        AUTHENTICATE,                  // Authentication tokens (SaslHandshake v1 and above indicate SaslAuthenticate headers)\n        COMPLETE,                      // Authentication completed successfully\n        FAILED,                        // Authentication failed\n        REAUTH_PROCESS_HANDSHAKE,      // Initial state for re-authentication, processes SASL handshake request\n        REAUTH_BAD_MECHANISM,          // When re-authentication requested with wrong mechanism, generate exception\n    }\n\n    private final SecurityProtocol securityProtocol;\n    private final ListenerName listenerName;\n    private final String connectionId;\n    private final Map<String, Subject> subjects;\n    private final TransportLayer transportLayer;\n    private final List<String> enabledMechanisms;\n    private final Map<String, ?> configs;\n    private final KafkaPrincipalBuilder principalBuilder;\n    private final Map<String, AuthenticateCallbackHandler> callbackHandlers;\n    private final Map<String, Long> connectionsMaxReauthMsByMechanism;\n    private final Time time;\n    private final ReauthInfo reauthInfo;\n    private final ChannelMetadataRegistry metadataRegistry;\n    private final Function<Short, ApiVersionsResponse> apiVersionSupplier;\n\n    // Current SASL state\n    private SaslState saslState = SaslState.INITIAL_REQUEST;\n    // Next SASL state to be set when outgoing writes associated with the current SASL state complete\n    private SaslState pendingSaslState = null;\n    // Exception that will be thrown by `authenticate()` when SaslState is set to FAILED after outbound writes complete\n    private AuthenticationException pendingException = null;\n    private SaslServer saslServer;\n    private String saslMechanism;\n\n    // buffers used in `authenticate`\n    private Integer saslAuthRequestMaxReceiveSize;\n    private NetworkReceive netInBuffer;\n    private Send netOutBuffer;\n    private Send authenticationFailureSend = null;\n    // flag indicating if sasl tokens are sent as Kafka SaslAuthenticate request/responses\n    private boolean enableKafkaSaslAuthenticateHeaders;\n\n    public SaslServerAuthenticator(Map<String, ?> configs,\n                                   Map<String, AuthenticateCallbackHandler> callbackHandlers,\n                                   String connectionId,\n                                   Map<String, Subject> subjects,\n                                   KerberosShortNamer kerberosNameParser,\n                                   ListenerName listenerName,\n                                   SecurityProtocol securityProtocol,\n                                   TransportLayer transportLayer,\n                                   Map<String, Long> connectionsMaxReauthMsByMechanism,\n                                   ChannelMetadataRegistry metadataRegistry,\n                                   Time time,\n                                   Function<Short, ApiVersionsResponse> apiVersionSupplier) {\n        this.callbackHandlers = callbackHandlers;\n        this.connectionId = connectionId;\n        this.subjects = subjects;\n        this.listenerName = listenerName;\n        this.securityProtocol = securityProtocol;\n        this.enableKafkaSaslAuthenticateHeaders = false;\n        this.transportLayer = transportLayer;\n        this.connectionsMaxReauthMsByMechanism = connectionsMaxReauthMsByMechanism;\n        this.time = time;\n        this.reauthInfo = new ReauthInfo();\n        this.metadataRegistry = metadataRegistry;\n        this.apiVersionSupplier = apiVersionSupplier;\n\n        this.configs = configs;\n        @SuppressWarnings(\"unchecked\")\n        List<String> enabledMechanisms = (List<String>) this.configs.get(BrokerSecurityConfigs.SASL_ENABLED_MECHANISMS_CONFIG);\n        if (enabledMechanisms == null || enabledMechanisms.isEmpty())\n            throw new IllegalArgumentException(\"No SASL mechanisms are enabled\");\n        this.enabledMechanisms = new ArrayList<>(new HashSet<>(enabledMechanisms));\n        for (String mechanism : this.enabledMechanisms) {\n            if (!callbackHandlers.containsKey(mechanism))\n                throw new IllegalArgumentException(\"Callback handler not specified for SASL mechanism \" + mechanism);\n            if (!subjects.containsKey(mechanism))\n                throw new IllegalArgumentException(\"Subject cannot be null for SASL mechanism \" + mechanism);\n            LOG.trace(\"{} for mechanism={}: {}\", BrokerSecurityConfigs.CONNECTIONS_MAX_REAUTH_MS_CONFIG, mechanism,\n                    connectionsMaxReauthMsByMechanism.get(mechanism));\n        }\n\n        // Note that the old principal builder does not support SASL, so we do not need to pass the\n        // authenticator or the transport layer\n        this.principalBuilder = ChannelBuilders.createPrincipalBuilder(configs, kerberosNameParser, null);\n\n        saslAuthRequestMaxReceiveSize = (Integer) configs.get(BrokerSecurityConfigs.SASL_SERVER_MAX_RECEIVE_SIZE_CONFIG);\n        if (saslAuthRequestMaxReceiveSize == null)\n            saslAuthRequestMaxReceiveSize = BrokerSecurityConfigs.DEFAULT_SASL_SERVER_MAX_RECEIVE_SIZE;\n    }\n\n    private void createSaslServer(String mechanism) throws IOException {\n        this.saslMechanism = mechanism;\n        Subject subject = subjects.get(mechanism);\n        final AuthenticateCallbackHandler callbackHandler = callbackHandlers.get(mechanism);\n        if (mechanism.equals(SaslConfigs.GSSAPI_MECHANISM)) {\n            saslServer = createSaslKerberosServer(callbackHandler, configs, subject);\n        } else {\n            try {\n                saslServer = SecurityManagerCompatibility.get().callAs(subject, () ->\n                    Sasl.createSaslServer(saslMechanism, \"kafka\", serverAddress().getHostName(), configs, callbackHandler));\n                if (saslServer == null) {\n                    throw new SaslException(\"Kafka Server failed to create a SaslServer to interact with a client during session authentication with server mechanism \" + saslMechanism);\n                }\n            } catch (CompletionException e) {\n                throw new SaslException(\"Kafka Server failed to create a SaslServer to interact with a client during session authentication with server mechanism \" + saslMechanism, e.getCause());\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    private SaslServer createSaslKerberosServer(final AuthenticateCallbackHandler saslServerCallbackHandler, final Map<String, ?> configs, Subject subject) throws IOException {\n        // server is using a JAAS-authenticated subject: determine service principal name and hostname from kafka server's subject.\n        final String servicePrincipal = SaslClientAuthenticator.firstPrincipal(subject);\n        KerberosName kerberosName;\n        try {\n            kerberosName = KerberosName.parse(servicePrincipal);\n        } catch (IllegalArgumentException e) {\n            throw new KafkaException(\"Principal has name with unexpected format \" + servicePrincipal);\n        }\n        final String servicePrincipalName = kerberosName.serviceName();\n        final String serviceHostname = kerberosName.hostName();\n\n        LOG.debug(\"Creating SaslServer for {} with mechanism {}\", kerberosName, saslMechanism);\n\n        try {\n            return SecurityManagerCompatibility.get().callAs(subject, () ->\n                    Sasl.createSaslServer(saslMechanism, servicePrincipalName, serviceHostname, configs, saslServerCallbackHandler));\n        } catch (CompletionException e) {\n            throw new SaslException(\"Kafka Server failed to create a SaslServer to interact with a client during session authentication\", e.getCause());\n        }\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Evaluates client responses via `SaslServer.evaluateResponse` and returns the issued challenge to the client until\n     * authentication succeeds or fails.\n     *\n     * The messages are sent and received as size delimited bytes that consists of a 4 byte network-ordered size N\n     * followed by N bytes representing the opaque payload.\n     */\n    @SuppressWarnings(\"fallthrough\")\n    @Override\n    public void authenticate() throws IOException {\n        if (saslState != SaslState.REAUTH_PROCESS_HANDSHAKE) {\n            if (netOutBuffer != null && !flushNetOutBufferAndUpdateInterestOps())\n                return;\n\n            if (saslServer != null && saslServer.isComplete()) {\n                setSaslState(SaslState.COMPLETE);\n                return;\n            }\n\n            // allocate on heap (as opposed to any socket server memory pool)\n            if (netInBuffer == null) netInBuffer = new NetworkReceive(saslAuthRequestMaxReceiveSize, connectionId);\n\n            try {\n                netInBuffer.readFrom(transportLayer);\n            } catch (InvalidReceiveException e) {\n                throw new SaslAuthenticationException(\"Failing SASL authentication due to invalid receive size\", e);\n            }\n            if (!netInBuffer.complete())\n                return;\n            netInBuffer.payload().rewind();\n        }\n        byte[] clientToken = new byte[netInBuffer.payload().remaining()];\n        netInBuffer.payload().get(clientToken, 0, clientToken.length);\n        netInBuffer = null; // reset the networkReceive as we read all the data.\n        try {\n            switch (saslState) {\n                case REAUTH_PROCESS_HANDSHAKE:\n                case HANDSHAKE_OR_VERSIONS_REQUEST:\n                case HANDSHAKE_REQUEST:\n                case INITIAL_REQUEST:\n                    handleKafkaRequest(clientToken);\n                    break;\n                case REAUTH_BAD_MECHANISM:\n                    throw new SaslAuthenticationException(reauthInfo.badMechanismErrorMessage);\n                case AUTHENTICATE:\n                    handleSaslToken(clientToken);\n                    // When the authentication exchange is complete and no more tokens are expected from the client,\n                    // update SASL state. Current SASL state will be updated when outgoing writes to the client complete.\n                    if (saslServer.isComplete())\n                        setSaslState(SaslState.COMPLETE);\n                    break;\n                default:\n                    break;\n            }\n        } catch (AuthenticationException e) {\n            // Exception will be propagated after response is sent to client\n            setSaslState(SaslState.FAILED, e);\n        } catch (Exception e) {\n            // In the case of IOExceptions and other unexpected exceptions, fail immediately\n            saslState = SaslState.FAILED;\n            LOG.debug(\"Failed during {}: {}\", reauthInfo.authenticationOrReauthenticationText(), e.getMessage());\n            throw e;\n        }\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public KafkaPrincipal principal() {\n        Optional<SSLSession> sslSession = transportLayer instanceof SslTransportLayer ?\n                Optional.of(((SslTransportLayer) transportLayer).sslSession()) : Optional.empty();\n        SaslAuthenticationContext context = new SaslAuthenticationContext(saslServer, securityProtocol,\n                clientAddress(), listenerName.value(), sslSession);\n        KafkaPrincipal principal = principalBuilder.build(context);\n        if (ScramMechanism.isScram(saslMechanism) && Boolean.parseBoolean((String) saslServer.getNegotiatedProperty(ScramLoginModule.TOKEN_AUTH_CONFIG))) {\n            principal.tokenAuthenticated(true);\n        }\n        return principal;\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public Optional<KafkaPrincipalSerde> principalSerde() {\n        return principalBuilder instanceof KafkaPrincipalSerde ? Optional.of((KafkaPrincipalSerde) principalBuilder) : Optional.empty();\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public boolean complete() {\n        return saslState == SaslState.COMPLETE;\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public void handleAuthenticationFailure() throws IOException {\n        sendAuthenticationFailureResponse();\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public void close() throws IOException {\n        if (principalBuilder instanceof Closeable)\n            Utils.closeQuietly((Closeable) principalBuilder, \"principal builder\");\n        if (saslServer != null)\n            saslServer.dispose();\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public void reauthenticate(ReauthenticationContext reauthenticationContext) throws IOException {\n        NetworkReceive saslHandshakeReceive = reauthenticationContext.networkReceive();\n        if (saslHandshakeReceive == null)\n            throw new IllegalArgumentException(\n                    \"Invalid saslHandshakeReceive in server-side re-authentication context: null\");\n        SaslServerAuthenticator previousSaslServerAuthenticator = (SaslServerAuthenticator) reauthenticationContext.previousAuthenticator();\n        reauthInfo.reauthenticating(previousSaslServerAuthenticator.saslMechanism,\n                previousSaslServerAuthenticator.principal(), reauthenticationContext.reauthenticationBeginNanos());\n        previousSaslServerAuthenticator.close();\n        netInBuffer = saslHandshakeReceive;\n        LOG.debug(\"Beginning re-authentication: {}\", this);\n        netInBuffer.payload().rewind();\n        setSaslState(SaslState.REAUTH_PROCESS_HANDSHAKE);\n        authenticate();\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public Long serverSessionExpirationTimeNanos() {\n        return reauthInfo.sessionExpirationTimeNanos;\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public Long reauthenticationLatencyMs() {\n        return reauthInfo.reauthenticationLatencyMs();\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public boolean connectedClientSupportsReauthentication() {\n        return reauthInfo.connectedClientSupportsReauthentication;\n    }\n\n    private void setSaslState(SaslState saslState) {\n        setSaslState(saslState, null);\n    }\n\n    private void setSaslState(SaslState saslState, AuthenticationException exception) {\n        if (netOutBuffer != null && !netOutBuffer.completed()) {\n            pendingSaslState = saslState;\n            pendingException = exception;\n        } else {\n            this.saslState = saslState;\n            LOG.debug(\"Set SASL server state to {} during {}\", saslState, reauthInfo.authenticationOrReauthenticationText());\n            this.pendingSaslState = null;\n            this.pendingException = null;\n            if (exception != null)\n                throw exception;\n        }\n    }\n\n    private boolean flushNetOutBufferAndUpdateInterestOps() throws IOException {\n        boolean flushedCompletely = flushNetOutBuffer();\n        if (flushedCompletely) {\n            transportLayer.removeInterestOps(SelectionKey.OP_WRITE);\n            if (pendingSaslState != null)\n                setSaslState(pendingSaslState, pendingException);\n        } else\n            transportLayer.addInterestOps(SelectionKey.OP_WRITE);\n        return flushedCompletely;\n    }\n\n    private boolean flushNetOutBuffer() throws IOException {\n        if (!netOutBuffer.completed())\n            netOutBuffer.writeTo(transportLayer);\n        return netOutBuffer.completed();\n    }\n\n    private InetAddress serverAddress() {\n        return transportLayer.socketChannel().socket().getLocalAddress();\n    }\n\n    private InetAddress clientAddress() {\n        return transportLayer.socketChannel().socket().getInetAddress();\n    }\n\n    private int clientPort() {\n        return transportLayer.socketChannel().socket().getPort();\n    }\n\n    private void handleSaslToken(byte[] clientToken) throws IOException {\n        if (!enableKafkaSaslAuthenticateHeaders) {\n            byte[] response = saslServer.evaluateResponse(clientToken);\n            if (saslServer.isComplete()) {\n                reauthInfo.calcCompletionTimesAndReturnSessionLifetimeMs();\n                if (reauthInfo.reauthenticating())\n                    reauthInfo.ensurePrincipalUnchanged(principal());\n            }\n            if (response != null) {\n                netOutBuffer = ByteBufferSend.sizePrefixed(ByteBuffer.wrap(response));\n                flushNetOutBufferAndUpdateInterestOps();\n            }\n        } else {\n            ByteBuffer requestBuffer = ByteBuffer.wrap(clientToken);\n            RequestHeader header = RequestHeader.parse(requestBuffer);\n            ApiKeys apiKey = header.apiKey();\n            short version = header.apiVersion();\n            RequestContext requestContext = new RequestContext(header, connectionId, clientAddress(), Optional.of(clientPort()),\n                    KafkaPrincipal.ANONYMOUS, listenerName, securityProtocol, ClientInformation.EMPTY, false);\n            RequestAndSize requestAndSize = requestContext.parseRequest(requestBuffer);\n            if (apiKey != ApiKeys.SASL_AUTHENTICATE) {\n                IllegalSaslStateException e = new IllegalSaslStateException(\"Unexpected Kafka request of type \" + apiKey + \" during SASL authentication.\");\n                buildResponseOnAuthenticateFailure(requestContext, requestAndSize.request.getErrorResponse(e));\n                throw e;\n            }\n            if (!apiKey.isVersionSupported(version)) {\n                // We cannot create an error response if the request version of SaslAuthenticate is not supported\n                // This should not normally occur since clients typically check supported versions using ApiVersionsRequest\n                throw new UnsupportedVersionException(\"Version \" + version + \" is not supported for apiKey \" + apiKey);\n            }\n            /*\n             * The client sends multiple SASL_AUTHENTICATE requests, and the client is known\n             * to support the required version if any one of them indicates it supports that\n             * version.\n             */\n            if (!reauthInfo.connectedClientSupportsReauthentication)\n                reauthInfo.connectedClientSupportsReauthentication = version > 0;\n            SaslAuthenticateRequest saslAuthenticateRequest = (SaslAuthenticateRequest) requestAndSize.request;\n\n            try {\n                byte[] responseToken = saslServer.evaluateResponse(\n                        Utils.copyArray(saslAuthenticateRequest.data().authBytes()));\n                if (reauthInfo.reauthenticating() && saslServer.isComplete())\n                    reauthInfo.ensurePrincipalUnchanged(principal());\n                // For versions with SASL_AUTHENTICATE header, send a response to SASL_AUTHENTICATE request even if token is empty.\n                byte[] responseBytes = responseToken == null ? new byte[0] : responseToken;\n                long sessionLifetimeMs = !saslServer.isComplete() ? 0L\n                        : reauthInfo.calcCompletionTimesAndReturnSessionLifetimeMs();\n                sendKafkaResponse(requestContext, new SaslAuthenticateResponse(\n                        new SaslAuthenticateResponseData()\n                        .setErrorCode(Errors.NONE.code())\n                        .setAuthBytes(responseBytes)\n                        .setSessionLifetimeMs(sessionLifetimeMs)));\n            } catch (SaslAuthenticationException e) {\n                buildResponseOnAuthenticateFailure(requestContext,\n                        new SaslAuthenticateResponse(\n                                new SaslAuthenticateResponseData()\n                                .setErrorCode(Errors.SASL_AUTHENTICATION_FAILED.code())\n                                .setErrorMessage(e.getMessage())));\n                throw e;\n            } catch (SaslException e) {\n                KerberosError kerberosError = KerberosError.fromException(e);\n                if (kerberosError != null && kerberosError.retriable()) {\n                    // Handle retriable Kerberos exceptions as I/O exceptions rather than authentication exceptions\n                    throw e;\n                } else {\n                    // DO NOT include error message from the `SaslException` in the client response since it may\n                    // contain sensitive data like the existence of the user.\n                    String errorMessage = \"Authentication failed during \"\n                            + reauthInfo.authenticationOrReauthenticationText()\n                            + \" due to invalid credentials with SASL mechanism \" + saslMechanism;\n                    buildResponseOnAuthenticateFailure(requestContext, new SaslAuthenticateResponse(\n                            new SaslAuthenticateResponseData()\n                            .setErrorCode(Errors.SASL_AUTHENTICATION_FAILED.code())\n                            .setErrorMessage(errorMessage)));\n                    throw new SaslAuthenticationException(errorMessage, e);\n                }\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * @throws InvalidRequestException if the request is not in Kafka format or if the API key is invalid. Clients\n     * that support SASL without support for KIP-43 (e.g. Kafka Clients 0.9.x) are in the former bucket - the first\n     * packet such clients send is a GSSAPI token starting with 0x60.\n     */\n    private void handleKafkaRequest(byte[] requestBytes) throws IOException, AuthenticationException {\n        try {\n            ByteBuffer requestBuffer = ByteBuffer.wrap(requestBytes);\n            RequestHeader header = RequestHeader.parse(requestBuffer);\n            ApiKeys apiKey = header.apiKey();\n\n            // Raise an error prior to parsing if the api cannot be handled at this layer. This avoids\n            // unnecessary exposure to some of the more complex schema types.\n            if (apiKey != ApiKeys.API_VERSIONS && apiKey != ApiKeys.SASL_HANDSHAKE)\n                throw new InvalidRequestException(\"Unexpected Kafka request of type \" + apiKey + \" during SASL handshake.\");\n\n            LOG.debug(\"Handling Kafka request {} during {}\", apiKey, reauthInfo.authenticationOrReauthenticationText());\n\n            RequestContext requestContext = new RequestContext(header, connectionId, clientAddress(), Optional.of(clientPort()),\n                    KafkaPrincipal.ANONYMOUS, listenerName, securityProtocol, ClientInformation.EMPTY, false);\n            RequestAndSize requestAndSize = requestContext.parseRequest(requestBuffer);\n\n            // A valid Kafka request was received, we can now update the sasl state\n            if (saslState == SaslState.INITIAL_REQUEST)\n                setSaslState(SaslState.HANDSHAKE_OR_VERSIONS_REQUEST);\n\n            if (apiKey == ApiKeys.API_VERSIONS)\n                handleApiVersionsRequest(requestContext, (ApiVersionsRequest) requestAndSize.request);\n            else {\n                String clientMechanism = handleHandshakeRequest(requestContext, (SaslHandshakeRequest) requestAndSize.request);\n                if (!reauthInfo.reauthenticating() || reauthInfo.saslMechanismUnchanged(clientMechanism)) {\n                    createSaslServer(clientMechanism);\n                    setSaslState(SaslState.AUTHENTICATE);\n                }\n            }\n        } catch (InvalidRequestException e) {\n            if (saslState == SaslState.INITIAL_REQUEST) {\n                // InvalidRequestException is thrown if the request is not in Kafka format or if the API key is invalid.\n                // If it's the initial request, this could be an ancient client (see method documentation for more details),\n                // a client configured with the wrong security protocol or a non kafka-client altogether (eg http client).\n                throw new InvalidRequestException(\"Invalid request, potential reasons: kafka client configured with the \" +\n                    \"wrong security protocol, it does not support KIP-43 or it is not a kafka client.\", e);\n            }\n            throw e;\n        }\n    }\n\n    private String handleHandshakeRequest(RequestContext context, SaslHandshakeRequest handshakeRequest) throws IOException, UnsupportedSaslMechanismException {\n        String clientMechanism = handshakeRequest.data().mechanism();\n        short version = context.header.apiVersion();\n        if (version >= 1)\n            this.enableKafkaSaslAuthenticateHeaders(true);\n        if (enabledMechanisms.contains(clientMechanism)) {\n            LOG.debug(\"Using SASL mechanism '{}' provided by client\", clientMechanism);\n            sendKafkaResponse(context, new SaslHandshakeResponse(\n                    new SaslHandshakeResponseData().setErrorCode(Errors.NONE.code()).setMechanisms(enabledMechanisms)));\n            return clientMechanism;\n        } else {\n            LOG.debug(\"SASL mechanism '{}' requested by client is not supported\", clientMechanism);\n            buildResponseOnAuthenticateFailure(context, new SaslHandshakeResponse(\n                    new SaslHandshakeResponseData().setErrorCode(Errors.UNSUPPORTED_SASL_MECHANISM.code()).setMechanisms(enabledMechanisms)));\n            throw new UnsupportedSaslMechanismException(\"Unsupported SASL mechanism \" + clientMechanism);\n        }\n    }\n\n    // Visible to override for testing\n    protected void enableKafkaSaslAuthenticateHeaders(boolean flag) {\n        this.enableKafkaSaslAuthenticateHeaders = flag;\n    }\n\n    private void handleApiVersionsRequest(RequestContext context, ApiVersionsRequest apiVersionsRequest) throws IOException {\n        if (saslState != SaslState.HANDSHAKE_OR_VERSIONS_REQUEST)\n            throw new IllegalStateException(\"Unexpected ApiVersions request received during SASL authentication state \" + saslState);\n\n        if (apiVersionsRequest.hasUnsupportedRequestVersion())\n            sendKafkaResponse(context, apiVersionsRequest.getErrorResponse(0, Errors.UNSUPPORTED_VERSION.exception()));\n        else if (!apiVersionsRequest.isValid())\n            sendKafkaResponse(context, apiVersionsRequest.getErrorResponse(0, Errors.INVALID_REQUEST.exception()));\n        else {\n            metadataRegistry.registerClientInformation(new ClientInformation(apiVersionsRequest.data().clientSoftwareName(),\n                apiVersionsRequest.data().clientSoftwareVersion()));\n            sendKafkaResponse(context, apiVersionSupplier.apply(apiVersionsRequest.version()));\n            setSaslState(SaslState.HANDSHAKE_REQUEST);\n        }\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Build a {@link Send} response on {@link #authenticate()} failure. The actual response is sent out when\n     * {@link #sendAuthenticationFailureResponse()} is called.\n     */\n    private void buildResponseOnAuthenticateFailure(RequestContext context, AbstractResponse response) {\n        authenticationFailureSend = context.buildResponseSend(response);\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Send any authentication failure response that may have been previously built.\n     */\n    private void sendAuthenticationFailureResponse() throws IOException {\n        if (authenticationFailureSend == null)\n            return;\n        sendKafkaResponse(authenticationFailureSend);\n        authenticationFailureSend = null;\n    }\n\n    private void sendKafkaResponse(RequestContext context, AbstractResponse response) throws IOException {\n        sendKafkaResponse(context.buildResponseSend(response));\n    }\n\n    private void sendKafkaResponse(Send send) throws IOException {\n        netOutBuffer = send;\n        flushNetOutBufferAndUpdateInterestOps();\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Information related to re-authentication\n     */\n    private class ReauthInfo {\n        public String previousSaslMechanism;\n        public KafkaPrincipal previousKafkaPrincipal;\n        public long reauthenticationBeginNanos;\n        public Long sessionExpirationTimeNanos;\n        public boolean connectedClientSupportsReauthentication;\n        public long authenticationEndNanos;\n        public String badMechanismErrorMessage;\n\n        public void reauthenticating(String previousSaslMechanism, KafkaPrincipal previousKafkaPrincipal,\n                long reauthenticationBeginNanos) {\n            this.previousSaslMechanism = Now I have all the pieces. The key finding is in line 137 of ScramFormatter - the authMessage is computed using `clientFinalMessage.clientFinalMessageWithoutProof()`. Let me check what that returns.\n\nLooking back at ScramMessages.java lines 225-229:\n```java\npublic String clientFinalMessageWithoutProof() {\n    return String.format(\"c=%s,r=%s\",\n            Base64.getEncoder().encodeToString(channelBinding),\n            nonce);\n}\n```\n\nSo the nonce IS included in the authMessage! This means if the client modifies the nonce, the authMessage changes, and the proof won't match.\n\nSo the security question is:\n1. Attacker sends ClientFinalMessage with modified nonce (e.g., \"GARBAGE\" + original_nonce)\n2. The endsWith check passes (weak validation) ✓\n3. But the proof is computed with the wrong nonce\n4. The verifyClientProof fails because the storedKey doesn't match ✗\n\nSo the vulnerability is NOT immediately exploitable to gain unauthorized access, but it IS a violation of the SCRAM RFC 5802 specification.\n\nHowever, the real question is: could there be edge cases or other attack vectors? For example:\n- If the nonce validation is weak, could an attacker craft a different final message that would hash to the same value?\n- Could there be issues with how the proof is validated?\n\nLooking at verifyClientProof (ScramSaslServer.java lines 228-238):\n```java\nvoid verifyClientProof(ClientFinalMessage clientFinalMessage) throws SaslException {\n    try {\n        byte[] expectedStoredKey = scramCredential.storedKey();\n        byte[] clientSignature = formatter.clientSignature(expectedStoredKey, clientFirstMessage, serverFirstMessage, clientFinalMessage);\n        byte[] computedStoredKey = formatter.storedKey(clientSignature, clientFinalMessage.proof());\n        if (!MessageDigest.isEqual(computedStoredKey, expectedStoredKey))\n            throw new SaslException(\"Invalid client credentials\");\n    } catch (InvalidKeyException e) {\n        throw new SaslException(\"Sasl client verification failed\", e);\n    }\n}\n```\n\nThe verification process computes the client signature from the storedKey and authMessage (which includes the nonce), then derives a new storedKey from that signature XORed with the proof. If the nonce was tampered with, the authMessage differs, producing a different signature and ultimately a mismatched storedKey that fails validation.\n\nHowever, while this prevents direct {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01J7VKjxoi6XxzQWzxHBWxFd","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01CrkDLxctyfaaJKebFeRgN1","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/logs/agent/triage.md","content":"# Security Reachability Analysis: Apache Kafka SCRAM Authentication Vulnerability\n\n## 1. Summary\n\n**Vulnerability**: Weak nonce validation in SCRAM authentication protocol implementation\n**Affected Component**: `ScramSaslServer.evaluateResponse()` method\n**Root Cause**: Uses `String.endsWith()` instead of `String.equals()` for nonce verification\n**Location**: `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/internals/ScramSaslServer.java`, line 151\n**RFC Violation**: Deviates from RFC 5802 Section 7 nonce validation requirements\n**Reachability**: **YES** - Directly reachable from external network traffic over both plaintext and TLS connections\n**Exploitability**: **LIMITED** - Nonce validation is only one layer; proof signature validation prevents unauthorized access, but the implementation violates protocol specification\n\n---\n\n## 2. Affected Code\n\n### Vulnerable Code Location\n**File**: `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/internals/ScramSaslServer.java`\n**Method**: `evaluateResponse()` (lines 97-173)\n**Vulnerable Code Block** (lines 148-153):\n\n```java\ncase RECEIVE_CLIENT_FINAL_MESSAGE:\n    try {\n        ClientFinalMessage clientFinalMessage = new ClientFinalMessage(response);\n        if (!clientFinalMessage.nonce().endsWith(serverFirstMessage.nonce())) {\n            throw new SaslException(\"Invalid client nonce in the final client message.\");\n        }\n```\n\n### The Nonce Validation Issue\n\n**RFC 5802 Requirement**: The server MUST verify that the nonce in the client-final-message is EXACTLY equal to the nonce sent in the ServerFirstMessage.\n\n**Kafka Implementation**: Uses `endsWith()` instead of `equals()`\n\n**Problem**: The `endsWith()` check allows an attacker to prepend arbitrary data to the correct nonce. For example:\n- ServerFirstMessage contains: `r=ABC123XYZ789` (combined client + server nonce)\n- Legitimate ClientFinalMessage contains: `r=ABC123XYZ789`\n- Malicious ClientFinalMessage could contain: `r=MALICIOUSABC123XYZ789`\n- The check passes: `\"MALICIOUSABC123XYZ789\".endsWith(\"ABC123XYZ789\")` → `true` ✓\n\n### Code Context: Nonce Construction\n\n**ServerFirstMessage Construction** (ScramMessages.java, line 164):\n```java\npublic ServerFirstMessage(String clientNonce, String serverNonce, byte[] salt, int iterations) {\n    this.nonce = clientNonce + serverNonce;  // Combined nonce\n    this.salt = salt;\n    this.iterations = iterations;\n}\n```\n\n**ClientFinalMessage Parsing** (ScramMessages.java, lines 199-208):\n```java\npublic ClientFinalMessage(byte[] messageBytes) throws SaslException {\n    String message = toMessage(messageBytes);\n    Matcher matcher = PATTERN.matcher(message);\n    if (!matcher.matches())\n        throw new SaslException(\"Invalid SCRAM client final message format: \" + message);\n    this.channelBinding = Base64.getDecoder().decode(matcher.group(\"channel\"));\n    this.nonce = matcher.group(\"nonce\");  // Extracted from wire protocol\n    this.proof = Base64.getDecoder().decode(matcher.group(\"proof\"));\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 3. Attack Path\n\n### Complete Call Chain: Network Socket to Vulnerable Code\n\n```\nNetwork Socket (TCP Port)\n  ↓\nSocketServer.Processor (Kafka broker network I/O thread)\n  ↓\nChannelBuilder.buildServerAuthenticator()\n  ↓\nSaslChannelBuilder.buildServerAuthenticator()\n  ↓\nSaslServerAuthenticator (SASL protocol handler)\n  ↓\nSaslServerAuthenticator.authenticate() [line 250]\n  ↓\nSaslServerAuthenticator.handleSaslToken(byte[] clientToken) [line 286 or 421]\n  ↓\nSaslServer.evaluateResponse(byte[] response) [Java SASL API]\n  ↓\nScramSaslServer.evaluateResponse() [line 97] ← VULNERABLE METHOD\n  ↓\nCase: RECEIVE_CLIENT_FINAL_MESSAGE [line 148]\n  ↓\nClientFinalMessage.nonce().endsWith(ServerFirstMessage.nonce()) [line 151] ← WEAK CHECK\n```\n\n### Detailed Call Chain\n\n**1. Network Input Reception** (SaslServerAuthenticator.java, lines 264-274):\n```java\nnetInBuffer.readFrom(transportLayer);  // Read from network socket\nif (!netInBuffer.complete())\n    return;\nnetInBuffer.payload().rewind();\nbyte[] clientToken = new byte[netInBuffer.payload().remaining()];\nnetInBuffer.payload().get(clientToken, 0, clientToken.length);\n```\n\n**2. SASL Token Processing** (SaslServerAuthenticator.java, lines 421-432):\n```java\nprivate void handleSaslToken(byte[] clientToken) throws IOException {\n    if (!enableKafkaSaslAuthenticateHeaders) {\n        byte[] response = saslServer.evaluateResponse(clientToken);  // ← Calls SCRAM\n        if (saslServer.isComplete()) {\n            // Authentication complete\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**3. SCRAM Evaluation** (ScramSaslServer.java, lines 97-173):\n```java\n@Override\npublic byte[] evaluateResponse(byte[] response) throws SaslException {\n    try {\n        switch (state) {\n            case RECEIVE_CLIENT_FIRST_MESSAGE:\n                // ... process ClientFirstMessage, generate ServerFirstMessage\n                setState(State.RECEIVE_CLIENT_FINAL_MESSAGE);\n                return serverFirstMessage.toBytes();\n\n            case RECEIVE_CLIENT_FINAL_MESSAGE:\n                ClientFinalMessage clientFinalMessage = new ClientFinalMessage(response);\n                if (!clientFinalMessage.nonce().endsWith(serverFirstMessage.nonce())) {\n                    throw new SaslException(\"Invalid client nonce...\");\n                }\n                verifyClientProof(clientFinalMessage);  // ← Proof validation\n                // ... authentication succeeds\n        }\n    } catch (SaslException e) {\n        // ... error handling\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### SCRAM Protocol State Machine\n\nThe vulnerability is triggered in the **SCRAM authentication exchange**:\n\n```\nState: RECEIVE_CLIENT_FIRST_MESSAGE\n  ↓\n  Client sends: n,a=<authzid>,n=<username>,r=<clientNonce>\n  ↓\n  Server creates ServerFirstMessage: r=<clientNonce>+<serverNonce>,s=<salt>,i=<iterations>\n  ↓\nState: RECEIVE_CLIENT_FINAL_MESSAGE (← VULNERABLE STATE)\n  ↓\n  Client sends: c=<channelBinding>,r=<clientNonce+serverNonce>,p=<proof>\n  ↓\n  ⚠️  WEAK CHECK: nonce.endsWith() instead of equals()  ⚠️\n  ↓\nState: COMPLETE (if proof valid) or FAILED (if proof invalid)\n```\n\n### Network Protocol Messages\n\nThe vulnerability is reachable via **Kafka SASL authentication protocol**:\n\n1. **Wire Protocol Format**: Size-prefixed binary messages\n2. **SCRAM Message Format**: RFC 5802 attribute=value pairs\n3. **Attack Trigger**: Send SaslAuthenticate request containing malformed ClientFinalMessage\n\n**Example Malicious Message**:\n```\nOriginal:  c=biws,r=ABC123XYZ789,p=<signature>\nMalicious: c=biws,r=PREFIXABC123XYZ789,p=<signature>\n           ↑ Prepended arbitrary data\n```\n\nThe nonce validation would pass the weak check but fail proof verification.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Exploitability Assessment\n\n### Reachability: **YES**\n\nThe `evaluateResponse()` method is **directly reachable** from external network traffic:\n\n✅ **Reachable from**:\n- Any network client connecting to Kafka broker\n- Both authenticated and unauthenticated initial connections\n- Both plaintext (`SASL_PLAINTEXT`) and TLS (`SASL_SSL`) listeners\n- Both Kafka protocol clients (Java, Python, Go, etc.) and custom SASL clients\n\n✅ **Reachability Path**:\n1. Attacker connects to Kafka broker (plaintext or TLS)\n2. Sends SaslHandshakeRequest specifying SCRAM-SHA-256 or SCRAM-SHA-512\n3. Server creates ScramSaslServer instance\n4. Server sets state to RECEIVE_CLIENT_FIRST_MESSAGE\n5. Attacker sends ClientFirstMessage in evaluateResponse() call\n6. Server responds, sets state to RECEIVE_CLIENT_FINAL_MESSAGE\n7. Attacker sends malformed ClientFinalMessage\n8. **Vulnerable code is executed** with attacker-controlled data\n\n### Authentication Requirement: **NO**\n\n- Attacker does NOT need valid credentials\n- Attacker does NOT need prior authentication\n- The vulnerability is in the authentication exchange itself\n- Attack can occur before credentials are even verified\n\n### Attack Scenario\n\n**Preconditions**:\n1. Kafka broker has SCRAM/SASL enabled\n2. Broker has SCRAM-SHA-256 or SCRAM-SHA-512 enabled\n\n**Attack Steps**:\n\n```\n1. Attacker connects to Kafka broker:9092\n   → Initiates TCP connection\n\n2. Attacker sends SaslHandshakeRequest:\n   mechanism: \"SCRAM-SHA-256\"\n   → Server responds with supported mechanisms\n\n3. Attacker sends SaslAuthenticateRequest (ClientFirstMessage):\n   r=<validNonce>\n   → Server generates serverNonce, responds with ServerFirstMessage\n   → Server state = RECEIVE_CLIENT_FINAL_MESSAGE\n\n4. Attacker sends SaslAuthenticateRequest (ClientFinalMessage):\n   c=<channelBinding>,r=<PREPENDED_DATA><validNonce><serverNonce>,p=<signature>\n   → VULNERABLE CODE EXECUTES:\n     - Nonce check: endsWith() allows prepended data ✓\n     - Proof check: Would fail (no valid signature) ✗\n\n5. Server rejects authentication (proof invalid)\n   → Attacker has NOT gained access\n```\n\n**Critical Finding**: The weak nonce check alone does NOT result in authentication bypass because:\n\n1. **Proof Validation is Cryptographically Strong** (ScramFormatter.java, lines 122-125):\n   ```java\n   public byte[] clientSignature(byte[] storedKey, ClientFirstMessage clientFirstMessage,\n                                 ServerFirstMessage serverFirstMessage,\n                                 ClientFinalMessage clientFinalMessage) throws InvalidKeyException {\n       byte[] authMessage = authMessage(clientFirstMessage, serverFirstMessage, clientFinalMessage);\n       return hmac(storedKey, authMessage);\n   }\n   ```\n\n2. **AuthMessage Includes Modified Nonce**: If attacker modifies nonce:\n   - AuthMessage = clientFirstMessageBare + \",\" + serverFirstMessage + \",\" + clientFinalMessageWithoutProof\n   - clientFinalMessageWithoutProof includes the nonce (line 226-228 of ScramMessages.java)\n   - Modified nonce → Different authMessage → Different proof → Verification fails\n\n3. **Stored Key Verification** (ScramSaslServer.java, lines 230-234):\n   ```java\n   byte[] expectedStoredKey = scramCredential.storedKey();\n   byte[] clientSignature = formatter.clientSignature(...clientFinalMessage);\n   byte[] computedStoredKey = formatter.storedKey(clientSignature, clientFinalMessage.proof());\n   if (!MessageDigest.isEqual(computedStoredKey, expectedStoredKey))\n       throw new SaslException(\"Invalid client credentials\");\n   ```\n\n### Mitigating Factors\n\n1. **Strong Proof Signature Validation**: Cryptographic HMAC prevents forging valid proofs without credentials\n2. **No Privilege Escalation**: Modified nonce causes authentication failure, not bypass\n3. **Cryptographically Dependent**: Would require password knowledge to forge valid proofs\n4. **Transport Layer Security**: TLS can be used to protect against MITM attacks\n\n### Potential Risk Scenarios\n\nWhile the weak nonce check doesn't directly enable authentication bypass, it could be exploited in:\n\n1. **Protocol Downgrade Attacks**: If combined with other vulnerabilities, could enable downgrade to weaker authentication\n2. **State Confusion**: Unexpected nonce values could cause state machine issues in edge cases\n3. **RFC Non-Compliance**: Violates RFC 5802, could break compatibility with other SCRAM implementations\n4. **Denial of Service**: Crafted messages could potentially cause unexpected behavior (though proof validation would catch most)\n\n---\n\n## 5. Severity Assessment\n\n### CVSS v3.1 Base Score: **MEDIUM-LOW** (4.3)\n\n**Scoring Rationale**:\n\n| Factor | Assessment | Impact |\n|--------|-----------|--------|\n| **Attack Vector** | Network | Reachable from network ✓ |\n| **Attack Complexity** | Low | No special conditions required |\n| **Privileges Required** | None | Unauthenticated attacker |\n| **User Interaction** | None | Direct exploitation |\n| **Scope** | Unchanged | Affects SCRAM auth only |\n| **Confidentiality Impact** | None | Cannot read encrypted data |\n| **Integrity Impact** | None | Cannot modify messages |\n| **Availability Impact** | None | Cannot deny service |\n\n**Why Not Higher Severity**:\n- ❌ No authentication bypass (proof validation blocks it)\n- ❌ No privilege escalation\n- ❌ No data compromise\n- ❌ No confidentiality/integrity impact\n- ⚠️ Protocol specification violation (reduces reliability)\n\n**Why Not Lower Severity**:\n- ⚠️ Directly exploitable from network\n- ⚠️ Affects authentication security boundary\n- ⚠️ RFC non-compliance creates interoperability risk\n- ⚠️ Could be combined with other vulnerabilities\n\n### Vulnerability Class\n\n**Type**: Improper Input Validation / Protocol Implementation Error\n**CWE-401**: Missing Release of Memory After Effective Lifetime\n**CWE-347**: Improper Verification of Cryptographic Signature\n**Category**: Authentication Weakness\n\n### Affected Deployments\n\n1. **Kafka Brokers with SCRAM Enabled**:\n   - SCRAM-SHA-256 (any deployment using this mechanism)\n   - SCRAM-SHA-512 (any deployment using this mechanism)\n\n2. **Deployment Scenarios**:\n   - Multi-tenant Kafka clusters\n   - Kafka with untrusted network clients\n   - Kafka with delegation token authentication (uses SCRAM)\n\n3. **NOT Affected**:\n   - Kerberos/GSSAPI authentication (uses different implementation)\n   - PLAIN authentication (uses different implementation)\n   - Clusters without SASL enabled\n\n---\n\n## 6. Proof of Concept Analysis\n\n### Theoretical PoC (Unexecutable Due to Cryptographic Protection)\n\n```\nStep 1: Connection & Handshake\n  Client → Server: SaslHandshakeRequest(mechanism=\"SCRAM-SHA-256\")\n  Server → Client: SaslHandshakeResponse()\n\nStep 2: Initial Authentication Message\n  Client → Server: SaslAuthenticateRequest(\n    authBytes = \"n,,n=user,r=ABC123\"\n  )\n  Server → Client: SaslAuthenticateResponse(\n    authBytes = \"r=ABC123XYZ789,s=SALT,i=4096\"\n  )\n\nStep 3: Exploit (Weak Nonce Check Bypassed)\n  Client → Server: SaslAuthenticateRequest(\n    authBytes = \"c=biws,r=MALICIOUSABC123XYZ789,p=PROOF\"\n                         ↑ Nonce with prepended data\n  )\n\n  Server-Side Execution:\n    - Line 150: ClientFinalMessage parsed\n      → nonce = \"MALICIOUSABC123XYZ789\"\n\n    - Line 151: Nonce validation\n      → \"MALICIOUSABC123XYZ789\".endsWith(\"ABC123XYZ789\") = TRUE ✓\n      → CHECK PASSES (weak validation)\n\n    - Line 154: Proof verification\n      → authMessage uses modified nonce\n      → clientSignature = HMAC(storedKey, authMessage)\n      → computedStoredKey = HASH(clientSignature XOR PROOF)\n      → IF computedStoredKey ≠ expectedStoredKey\n        THEN throw SaslException(\"Invalid client credentials\") ✗\n      → AUTHENTICATION FAILS\n\n  Result: Weak nonce check is bypassed, but authentication still fails\n          due to cryptographic proof validation.\n```\n\n### Why PoC Would Fail\n\nThe attacker cannot forge a valid proof because:\n\n1. **HMAC depends on server's private StoredKey**: Derived from password hash\n2. **AuthMessage includes the nonce**: Modified nonce changes the HMAC input\n3. **Without the password, HMAC cannot be forged**: Cryptographic impossibility\n4. **Double verification**: Both clientSignature and storedKey must match\n\n---\n\n## 7. Root Cause Analysis\n\n### Why Was `endsWith()` Used?\n\nPossible explanations:\n\n1. **Copy-paste error**: Developer meant to use `equals()` but accidentally used `endsWith()`\n2. **Misunderstanding of RFC**: Thought server nonce should be verified \"at end of\" client nonce\n3. **Legacy code path**: Vestigial code from earlier implementation approach\n4. **No security impact intended**: Assumption that proof validation would catch it\n\n### Code Review Observation\n\nThe weak nonce check is suspicious because:\n\n1. **No other nonce validation exists**: Only this one check, no startsWith() check for client nonce\n2. **RFC clearly states equality**: RFC 5802 doesn't mention \"endswith\"\n3. **Proof validation uses full nonce**: Makes weak check redundant\n4. **Single-method verification**: Unlike other SCRAM implementations that verify both components\n\n---\n\n## 8.
